Documentation

The friendly Operating System for the Internet of Things

    doc/doxygen/src/changelog.md
    1 Changelog {#changelog}
    2 =========
    3 
    4 [TOC]
    5 
    6 # Release 2020.04 {#release-2020-04}
    7 
    8  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    9  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    10  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    11  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    12 
    13  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    14  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    15  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    16 
    17  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    18  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    19  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    20  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    21 
    22  About this release:
    23  ===================
    24 
    25  The 2020.04 release includes:
    26 
    27  - Add support for 6LoWPAN IPv6 extension header next header compression
    28  - Add support for DHCPv6 prefix delegation client
    29  - Add support for kw41zrf and at86rf215 IEEE 802.15.4 radios
    30  - Improvements on power management for ESP32
    31  - Improvements and extensions in support of fe310 and lpc2387
    32  - lwIP: provide support for asynchronous sock
    33  - Improvements on xtimer module and testing
    34  - Initial addition of the new timer subsystem: ztimer
    35  - Migration to Kconfig - phase I: add multiple GNRC and system modules
    36  - +10 new boards, +11 new drivers, +7 new packages
    37 
    38  555 pull requests, composed of 1514 commits, have been merged since the
    39  last release, and 22 issues have been solved. 60 people contributed with
    40  code in 102 days. 3346 files have been touched with 358398 (+) insertions and
    41  184720 deletions (-).
    42 
    43  Notations used below:
    44  =====================
    45 
    46  + means new feature/item
    47  * means modified feature/item
    48  - means removed feature/item

    53  System libraries
    54  ----------------
    55  * core:

    343  Kconfig migration
    344  -----------------
    345  Migration to Kconfig as configuration tool is currently on phase 1. Which means
    346  that we are moving configuration options from modules to Kconfig files, and
    347  leaving its use optional.
    348 
    349  + doc: add Kconfig section

    351  * add CPU and Board common symbols
    352  * add Drivers menu

    489  Deprecations
    490  ============
    491 
    492  Warnings
    493  --------
    494  - `make all-debug` target will be removed for `native` after the 2020.10 release
    495  - net/gcoap: `gcoap_add_qstring()` will be removed after the 2020.10 release
    496  - net/gnrc/nettype: `GNRC_NETTYPE_IOVEC` type will be removed after 2020.10
    497  release
    498  - net/gnrc_pktbuf: `gnrc_pktbuf_replace_snip()` will be removed after 2020.10
    499  release
    500  - net/gnrc/sixlowpan: Configuration macro
    501  `GNRC_SIXLOWPAN_FRAG_RBUF_AGGRESSIVE_OVERRIDE` will be removed after 2020.10
    502  release.
    503 
    504  Removals
    505  --------
    506  - Makefile.include: remove support for GNU make <4
    507  - pkg/oonf_api: remove package
    508  - pkg/tinydtls: remove TINYDTLS_LOG configuration macro
    509  - sys/net/gnrc_tftp: remove module
    510  - sys/net/nhdp: remove module

    522  sometimes

    525  #12943: driver/mrf24j40: blocks shell input with auto_init_gnrc_netif
    526  #12884: examples/cord_ep: Dead lock when (re-)registering in callback function
    527  #12858: KW2XRF: Broken network communication without netstats-l2
    528  #12857: examples/gnrc_networking_mac broken on ATmega

    768 
    769 # Release 2020.01 {#release-2020-01}
    770 
    771  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    772  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    773  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    774  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    775 
    776  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    777  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    778  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    779 
    780  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    781  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    782  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    783  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    784 
    785  About this release:
    786  ===================
    787 
    788  The 2020.01 release includes:
    789 
    790  - Initial support for MicroPython
    791  - Initial support for GNRC based LoRaWAN stack
    792  - Initial (experimental) asynchronous sock support
    793  - Extend support for lpc2387 and fe310 cpus
    794  - Xtimer concurrency/robustness improvement, fixing #8388, #5338 & #5103
    795  - Complete re-implementation of esp8266 based on ESP8266 RTOS SDK
    796  - Improvements in automatic tests
    797  - Introduce and start using Kconfig as a configuration tool
    798  - +12 new boards, +7 new drivers, +4 new packages
    799 
    800  About 527 pull requests, composed of 1367 commits, have been merged since the
    801  last release, and about 29 issues have been solved. 61 people contributed with
    802  code in 111 days. Approximately 3053 files have been touched with 134416 (+)
    803  insertions and 31870 deletions (-).
    804

    809  - means removed feature/item

    1105  API Changes
    1106  ===========
    1107 
    1108  - drivers/ina220: changes to comply with RIOT's design goals & SAUL adaption
    1109  - usbus: unified terminology within USBUS to match the terminology from the
    1110  specs. `hdr`, `hdrs`, `headers`, etc is replaced everywhere with `descr`
    1111  `descriptors` and `descriptors`.
    1112  - Makefile.include: fail by default when errors are expected
    1113 
    1114  ```diff
    1115  /* change return type of `adc_sample()` to `int32_t` to allow support for ADCs
    1116  with resolution of more than 16 bits on 8 bit and 16 bit platforms*/
    1117  - int adc_sample(adc_t line, adc_res_t res)
    1118  = int32_t adc_sample(adc_t line, adc_res_t res)
    1119 
    1120  /* pass memo to resp_handler directly */
    1121  - typedef void (*gcoap_resp_handler_t)(unsigned req_state, coap_pkt_t* pdu,
    1122  - sock_udp_ep_t *remote);
    1123  + typedef void (*gcoap_resp_handler_t)(const gcoap_request_memo_t *memo,
    1124  + coap_pkt_t* pdu,
    1125  + const sock_udp_ep_t *remote);
    1126 
    1127  /* allow to pass user context to requests */
    1128  size_t gcoap_req_send(const uint8_t *buf, size_t len,
    1129  const sock_udp_ep_t *remote,
    1130  - gcoap_resp_handler_t resp_handler);
    1131  + gcoap_resp_handler_t resp_handler, void *context);
    1132 
    1133  /* assume `netif->ops->init()` to be set to at least a default */
    1134  - _init_from_device(netif);
    1135  - #ifdef DEVELHELP
    1136  - _test_options(netif);
    1137  + netif->ops->init(netif);
    1138  + #if DEVELHELP
    1139  + assert(options_tested);
    1140  # endif
    1141  - netif->cur_hl = GNRC_NETIF_DEFAULT_HL;
    1142  - #ifdef MODULE_GNRC_IPV6_NIB
    1143  - gnrc_ipv6_nib_init_iface(netif);
    1144  - #endif
    1145  - if (netif->ops->init) {
    1146  - netif->ops->init(netif);
    1147  - }
    1148 
    1149  /* split the semantic of gnrc_netif_is_6ln() into two check functions */
    1150  /* is the interface performing 6Lo-ND as specified in RFC 6775. */
    1151  - bool gnrc_netif_is_6ln(const gnrc_netif_t *netif);
    1152  + bool gnrc_netif_is_6lo(const gnrc_netif_t *netif);
    1153  + static inline bool gnrc_netif_is_6ln(const gnrc_netif_t *netif
    1154 
    1155  /* add function to start a shell and exit once EOF is reached. */
    1156  + void shell_run_once(const shell_command_t *commands, char *line_buf, int len);
    1157 
    1158  /* return reassembly buffer entry created or updated */
    1159  - void gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_add(gnrc_netif_hdr_t *netif_hdr,
    1160  - gnrc_pktsnip_t *frag, size_t offset,
    1161  - unsigned page);
    1162  + gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_t *gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_add(gnrc_netif_hdr_t *netif_hdr,
    1163  + gnrc_pktsnip_t *frag,
    1164  + size_t offset, unsigned page);
    1165 
    1166  /* move gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_dispatch_when_complete() out of
    1167  gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_add(). The caller of the latter function is now
    1168  responsible to call it. */
    1169  + int gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_dispatch_when_complete(gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_t *rbuf,
    1170  + gnrc_netif_hdr_t *netif);
    1171 
    1172  /* don't assume interface specifier is an int for splitting, add functions to
    1173  split int and string */
    1174  - * @return interface number or -1 if none specified
    1175  + * @return string containing the interface specifier.
    1176  + * @return NULL if no interface was specified.
    1177  + */
    1178  - static inline int ipv6_addr_split_iface(char *addr_str)
    1179  + static inline char *ipv6_addr_split_iface(char *addr_str)
    1180 
    1181  - int ipv6_addr_split(char *addr_str, char seperator, int _default);
    1182  + int ipv6_addr_split_int(char *addr_str, char seperator, int _default);
    1183  + char *ipv6_addr_split_str(char *addr_str, char separator);
    1184 
    1185  /* change address getter and setter functions to avoid byte order confusion */
    1186  - uint16_t at86rf2xx_get_addr_short(const at86rf2xx_t *dev);
    1187  + void at86rf2xx_get_addr_short(const at86rf2xx_t *dev, network_uint16_t *addr);
    1188 
    1189  - void at86rf2xx_set_addr_short(at86rf2xx_t *dev, uint16_t addr);
    1190  + void at86rf2xx_set_addr_short(at86rf2xx_t *dev, const network_uint16_t *addr);
    1191 
    1192  - uint64_t at86rf2xx_get_addr_long(const at86rf2xx_t *dev);
    1193  + void at86rf2xx_get_addr_long(const at86rf2xx_t *dev, eui64_t *addr);
    1194 
    1195  - void at86rf2xx_set_addr_long(at86rf2xx_t *dev, uint64_t addr);
    1196  + void at86rf2xx_set_addr_long(at86rf2xx_t *dev, const eui64_t *addr);
    1197  ```

    1460  License
    1461  =======
    1462  * The code developed by the RIOT community is licensed under the GNU Lesser
    1463  General Public License (LGPL) version 2.1 as published by the Free Software

    1468 
    1469 # Release 2019.10 {#release-2019-10}
    1470 
    1471  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    1472  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    1473  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    1474  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    1475 
    1476  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    1477  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    1478  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    1479 
    1480  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    1481  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    1482  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    1483  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    1484 
    1485  About this release:
    1486  ===================
    1487 
    1488  The 2019.10 release includes:
    1489 
    1490  - initial support for SUIT firmware updates
    1491  - USB CDC-ACM serial communication
    1492  - complete rewrite of TI CC110x radio driver
    1493  - initial support for IPv6 fragmentation
    1494  - DTLS support in the sock networking stack
    1495  - complete blockwise messaging for gcoap and nanocoap
    1496  - as always, bug fixes and documentation updates
    1497 
    1498  About 460 pull requests, composed of 950 commits, have been merged since the
    1499  last release, and about 60 issues have been solved. 57 people contributed with
    1500  code in 105 days. Approximately 2000 files have been touched with 129000
    1501  insertions and 25000 deletions.
    1502 
    1503  Notations used below:
    1504  =====================
    1505  + means new feature/item
    1506  * means modified feature/item
    1507  - means removed feature/item

    1663  API Changes
    1664  ========================
    1665 
    1666  ```
    1667  /* no error handling possible, so no need to return a value */
    1668  - int i2c_release(i2c_t dev)
    1669  + void i2c_release(i2c_t dev)
    1670 
    1671  /* return 0 on success, rather than 1; so like timer_init() */
    1672  int timer_set(tim_t dev, int channel, unsigned int timeout)
    1673  int timer_set_absolute(tim_t dev, int channel, unsigned int value)
    1674  int timer_clear(tim_t dev, int channel)
    1675 
    1676  /* implementations already cast the argument to uint8_t* internally, so not
    1677  a significant semantic change */
    1678  - size_t eeprom_read(uint32_t pos, uint8_t *data, size_t len)
    1679  + size_t eeprom_read(uint32_t pos, void *data, size_t len)
    1680 
    1681  - size_t eeprom_write(uint32_t pos, const uint8_t *data, size_t len)
    1682  + size_t eeprom_write(uint32_t pos, const void *data, size_t len)
    1683 
    1684  /* now returns CIPHER_ERR_INVALID_KEY_SIZE on invalid keySize */
    1685  int aes_init(cipher_context_t *context, const uint8_t *key, uint8_t keySize)
    1686 
    1687  /* add setter for netif of interface header */
    1688  + void gnrc_netif_hdr_set_netif(gnrc_netif_hdr_t *hdr, const gnrc_netif_t *netif)
    1689 
    1690  ```

    1982 
    1983 # Release 2019.07 {#release-2019-07}
    1984 
    1985  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    1986  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    1987  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    1988  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    1989 
    1990  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    1991  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    1992  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    1993 
    1994  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    1995  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    1996  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    1997  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    1998 
    1999  About this release:
    2000  ===================
    2001 
    2002  The 2019.07 release includes a number of new features including many new
    2003  boards and cpu, riotboot added to many new and old boards, USB is now available,
    2004  BLE improvements, Ethernet on stm32 platforms, as well as many bug fixes and
    2005  documentation updates. Testing has also improved with both On-Target Testing
    2006  increasing and now Hardware Assisted Automated Tests being run.
    2007 
    2008  About 300 pull requests with about 659 commits have been merged since the last
    2009  release and about 50 issues have been solved. 26 people contributed with code
    2010  in 106 days. Approximately 1377 files have been touched with 181993 insertions
    2011  and 19668 deletions.
    2012

    2489 
    2490 # Release 2019.04 {#release-2019-04}
    2491 
    2492  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    2493  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    2494  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    2495  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    2496 
    2497  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    2498  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    2499  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    2500 
    2501  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    2502  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    2503  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    2504  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    2505 
    2506  About this release:
    2507  ===================
    2508 
    2509  The 2019.04 release includes a number of new features including porting of
    2510  riotboot to a number of new platforms, 802.15.4 support on the nRF52, and the
    2511  ability for firmware to flash images into a separate boot slot. Support for
    2512  several new boards and new sensors was added. Additionally, this release
    2513  contains a number of bug fixes and test improvements.
    2514 
    2515  About 320 pull requests with about 569 commits have been merged since the last
    2516  release and about 40 issues have been solved. 44 people contributed with code
    2517  in 88 days. Approximately 825 files have been touched with 32716 insertions
    2518  and 5149 deletions.
    2519 
    2520  Notations used below:
    2521  =====================
    2522  + means new feature/item
    2523  * means modified feature/item
    2524  - means removed feature/item
    2525 
    2526  New features and changes
    2527  ========================
    2528 
    2529  System libraries
    2530  ----------------
    2531  + riotboot_flashwrite: added module to reliably write a firmware image to
    2532  flash
    2533  + crypto: added support for chacha20poly1305 AEAD symmetric key cypher
    2534  algorithm
    2535  * threads: added usage of thread_state_t enum to define thread states,
    2536  instead of an integer
    2537  * random: added usage of hwrng as seed if available
    2538  + app_metadata: added module to print application metadata
    2539  + unaligned.h: added functions to safely read values from potentially
    2540  unaligned pointers
    2541  + isrpipe: split isrpipe_read_timeout to isolate xtimer dependency
    2542 
    2543  Networking
    2544  ----------
    2545  * gnrc_ipv6: adapted ping6 to original-ping-like implementation
    2546  * gnrc_ipv6: allowed sending empty IPv6 packets
    2547  + gnrc_netif_ieee802154: optional support to drop duplicate broadcast
    2548  packets
    2549  - gnrc_pktbuf: removed deprecated gnrc_pktbuf_get_iovec() function
    2550  + l2util: initial import of a general IPv6 over X helper module
    2551  + NimBLE: added Bluetooth device scanner
    2552  + NimBLE: added helper functions for address printing
    2553  * NimBLE: updated package to the latest version
    2554 
    2555  Packages
    2556  --------
    2557  + c25519: add support (embedded x25519 crypto library)
    2558 
    2559  Boards
    2560  ------
    2561  + Arduino nano: added support
    2562  + nrf52832-mdk: added support
    2563  + PhyTec reel board: added support
    2564  + MicroPython pyboard v1.1: added support
    2565  + Hamilton: added support
    2566  + saml10-xpro and saml11-xpro: added riotboot support
    2567  + nrf52: added riotboot support
    2568  + ESP32 and stm32: added command to allow runtime configuration of uart mode
    2569  + ESP32 and ESP8266: add support for ESP-NOW network device driver
    2570  * ESP8266: freed up RAM by moving most .rodata sections from DRAM to IROM
    2571  + Arduino: added test to verify pin mappings
    2572  + b-l072z-lrwan1: enabled RTT feature
    2573  + STM32l0: added support for dual bank flashing with OpenOCD
    2574  * Autonomo: changed flasher to BOSSA
    2575  * stm32: rework common clock configuration for stm32f4
    2576  * stm32f3discovery: Fix no external low speed crystal
    2577 
    2578  CPU
    2579  ---
    2580  + stm32l0: added riotboot support
    2581  + stm32f0: added support for periph_pm
    2582  + stm32f3, f7, l1 and l4: added stop and standby low power modes. All
    2583  STM32 families now provide periph_pm
    2584  + samd21: enabled idle modes
    2585  + sam0: added support for RWWEE on-chip memory
    2586  + Kinetis: added support for EA series and S9KEAZ129 MCU
    2587  + TI CC2650: added I2C periph implementation

    2595  + nrf52: added initial 802.15.4 support
    2596  + add7746 capacitance sensor: added driver

    2864 # Release 2019.01 {#release-2019-01}
    2865 
    2866  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    2867  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    2868  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    2869  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    2870 
    2871  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    2872  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    2873  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    2874 
    2875  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    2876  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    2877  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    2878  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    2879 
    2880  About this release:
    2881  ===================
    2882 
    2883  The 2019.01 release includes a number of new features including DMA support on
    2884  all STM32 boards, WiFi with IP connectivity on ESP32 and ESP8266, and riotboot,
    2885  a simple bootloader supporting multiple firmware slots, compatible with most Arm
    2886  Cortex-M boards supported by RIOT. Support for several new boards and new sensors
    2887  was added, as well as for the new CPU architecture Armv8-M (Cortex-M23). Last
    2888  but not least, this release contains a number of bug fixes and enhances test
    2889  automation.
    2890 
    2891  About 387 pull requests with about 912 commits have been merged since the last
    2892  release and about 36 issues have been solved. 54 people contributed with code
    2893  in 110 days. Approximately 1554 files have been touched with 176241 insertions
    2894  and 50593 deletions.
    2895

    3239 # Release 2018.10 {#release-2018-10}
    3240 
    3241  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    3242  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    3243  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    3244  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    3245 
    3246  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    3247  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    3248  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    3249 
    3250  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    3251  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    3252  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    3253  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    3254 
    3255  About this release:
    3256  ===================
    3257 
    3258  The 2018.10 release includes new features, like CoAP Resource Directory and
    3259  Block2, ESP32 support, rework of I2C interface, EEPROM registry,
    3260  Full and Minimal Thread Devices support in OpenThread and compliance of
    3261  LoRaWAN 1.0.2 (ABP counters stored in EEPROM). Several boards were introduced.
    3262 
    3263  During the last release the board documentation was migrated from the wiki to
    3264  the [RIOT API documentation](https://doc.riot-os.org) to improve the
    3265  maintenance of these entries and provide a better user experience when
    3266  browsing the documentation. There were also some efforts in grouping some
    3267  modules to make them easier to access in the documentation.
    3268 
    3269  There were also some efforts on refactoring, test improvements and bug fixes.
    3270 
    3271  About 392 pull requests with about 914 commits have been merged since the last
    3272  release and about 20 issues have been solved. 57 people contributed with code
    3273  in 100 days. Approximately 2184 files have been touched with 211964 insertions
    3274  and 34806 deletions.
    3275 
    3276  Notations used below:
    3277  =====================
    3278  + means new feature/item
    3279  * means modified feature/item
    3280  - means removed feature/item

    3612 
    3613 # Release 2018.07 {#release-2018-07}
    3614 
    3615  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    3616  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    3617  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    3618  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    3619 
    3620  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    3621  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    3622  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    3623 
    3624  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    3625  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    3626  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    3627  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    3628 
    3629  About this release:
    3630  ===================
    3631 
    3632  The 2018.07 release includes new features, like NimBLE (ble stack),
    3633  a MQTT-SN client, SHA-1 based PRNG, an UUID implementation. The RISC-V CPU
    3634  architecture support used by the hifive1 board.
    3635  Effort was done on refactoring, documentation, test improvements and bug fixes.
    3636 
    3637  During the last release, maintainers contributed by running the automated test
    3638  suites on their boards. This gave valuable feedback on the board support state,
    3639  test reliability and where to focus effort to make testing easier and more
    3640  reliable.
    3641 
    3642  About 380 pull requests with about 675 commits have been merged since the last
    3643  release and about 27 issues have been solved. 45 people contributed with code
    3644  in 93 days. Approximately 1678 files have been touched with 147122 insertions
    3645  and 16060 deletions.
    3646

    3893 # Release 2018.04 {#release-2018-04}
    3894 
    3895  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    3896  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    3897  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    3898  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    3899 
    3900  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    3901  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    3902  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    3903 
    3904  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    3905  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    3906  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    3907  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    3908 
    3909  About this release:
    3910  ===================
    3911  The 2018.04 release includes major progress in support for current crypto
    3912  libraries. A lot of work has gone into updating drivers to RIOT's unified
    3913  configuration scheme. Support for ten new boards has been added. In our quest
    3914  to improve and automate testing, many test scripts have been fixed and
    3915  improved, and RIOT's CI now runs many tests on real hardware during its nightly
    3916  build testing. And as usual, many tiny fixes and improvements have been merged.
    3917 
    3918  About 390 pull requests with about 1073 commits have been merged since the last
    3919  release and about 54 issues have been solved. 44 people contributed with code
    3920  in 98 days. Approximately 1491 files have been touched with 208426 insertions.
    3921 
    3922  Notations used below:
    3923  =====================
    3924  + means new feature/item
    3925  * means modified feature/item
    3926  - means removed feature/item
    3927

    3933  + hashes: add sha-3 implementation
    3934

    3938  + nanocoap: added server-side block1 support
    3939  + skald: a BLE advertising stack
    3940

    3942  --------
    3943  + cayenne-lpp: A Cayenne LPP library written in C
    3944  + HACL*: a formally verified cryptographic library written in F*
    3945  + qDSA: Small and Secure Digital Signatures with Curve-based
    3946  Diffie--Hellman Key Pairs
    3947  + libcose: Constrained node COSE library
    3948  + cn-cbor: A constrained node implementation of CBOR in C
    3949  + ucglib

    4018 # Release 2018.01 {#release-2018-01}
    4019 
    4020  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    4021  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    4022  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit and 16-bit microcontrollers as well as
    4023  light-weight 32-bit processors.
    4024 
    4025  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    4026  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    4027  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    4028 
    4029  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    4030  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    4031  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    4032  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    4033 
    4034  About this release:
    4035  ===================
    4036  The 2018.01 release includes major progress in RIOTs network communication
    4037  capabilities, i.e., rewrite of GNRC's neighbour discovery, confirmable messages
    4038  in (g)CoAP, LoRa, and GoMacH as well as updates on CCN-lite and LWIP.
    4039  Furthermore, RIOT contributes to _IKEA-Hacking_ by bringing support for
    4040  the smart home lighting system TRADFRI (note: this will void the warranty).
    4041  Needless to say that this release also adds and updates support for several
    4042  platforms, drivers, and of course lots of enhancements to the documentation
    4043  as well as numerous bug fixes. Last but not least, RIOT now has an official
    4044  code of conduct (https://github.com/RIOT-OS/RIOT/blob/master/CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md)
    4045 
    4046  More than 442 pull requests with about 865 commits have been merged since the
    4047  last release and about 96 issues have been solved. 54 people contributed with code
    4048  in 96 days. Approximately 2370 files have been touched with 223970 insertions
    4049  and 181409 deletions.
    4050

    4217 # Release 2017.10 {#release-2017-10}
    4218 
    4219  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    4220  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    4221  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit microcontrollers, 16-bit
    4222  microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    4223 
    4224  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    4225  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    4226  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    4227 
    4228  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    4229  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    4230  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    4231  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    4232 
    4233  About this release:
    4234  ===================
    4235  Most notable, this release is bringing RIOT a step closer to supporting
    4236  over-the-air-updates by containing initial support for MCUBoot.
    4237  Furthermore, it adds support for some new platforms (e.g. arduino-mkzero,
    4238  nucleos, and frdm-k22f), drivers (e.g. my9221, apa102, ds1307), and of course
    4239  a large number of bug fixes (e.g. `make buildtest` now working properly,
    4240  various fixes to `xtimer`).
    4241 
    4242  About 390 pull requests with about 500 commits have been merged since the last
    4243  release and about 60 issues have been solved. 39 people contributed with code
    4244  in 113 days. 1825 files have been touched with 223454 insertions and 66146 deletions.

    4321  #5460: cpu/samd21: i2c timing with compiler optimization
    4322  #5489: cpu/lpc11u34: ADC broken
    4323  #5799: kw2x: 15.4 duplicate transmits
    4324  #5928: xtimer: usage in board_init() crashes: some boards use the xtimer in there board_init()
    4325  function. The xtimer is however first initialized in the auto_init module which is executed
    4326  after board_init()
    4327  #6022: pkg: build order issue
    4328  #6331: RTC alarm triggered with 1s delay
    4329  #6419: cpu/cc2538: timer broken
    4330  #6427: xtimer: infinite loop with xtimer_mutex_lock_timeout
    4331  #6501: boards/nucleo: Pin usage collision (SPI clk vs. LED0)
    4332  #6542: boards/nucle-f0xx: misconfigured timer configuration
    4333  #6904: cpu/saml21: cannot use several EXTI
    4334 
    4335  Known Issues
    4336  ============
    4337  Networking related issues
    4338  -------------------------
    4339  #3075: nhdp: unnecessary microsecond precision: NHDP works with timer values of microsecond precision
    4340  which is not required. Changing to lower precision would save some memory.
    4341  #4048: gnrc: potential racey memory leak
    4342  #5016: gnrc_rpl: Rejoining RPL instance as root after reboot messes up routing
    4343  #5230: gnrc ipv6: multicast packets are not dispatched to the upper layers
    4344  #5656: Possible Weakness with locking in the GNRC network stack: For some operations mutexes to the
    4345  network interfaces need to get unlocked in the current implementation to not get deadlocked.
    4346  Recursive mutexes as provided in #5731 might help to solve this problem.
    4347  #5748: gnrc: nodes crashing with too small packet buffer: A packet buffer of size ~512 B might lead
    4348  to crashes. The issue describes this for several hundret nodes, but agressive flooding with
    4349  just two nodes was also shown to lead to this problem.
    4350  #5858: gnrc: 6lo: potential problem with reassembly of fragments: If one frame gets lost the reassembly
    4351  state machine might get out of sync
    4352  #6123: gnrc: crash with (excessive) traffic
    4353  #7035: lwIP: hangs due to sema change after a while
    4354  #7737: pkg: libcoap is partially broken and outdated
    4355 
    4356  NDP is not working properly
    4357  ---------------------------
    4358  #4499: handle of l2src_len in gnrc_ndp_rtr_sol_handle: Reception of a router solicitation might lead
    4359  to invalid zero-length link-layer addresses in neighbor cache.
    4360  #5005: ndp: router advertisement sent with global address: Under some circumstances a router might
    4361  send RAs with GUAs. While they are ignored on receive (as RFC-4861 specifies), RAs should have
    4362  link-local addresses and not even be send out this way.
    4363  #5122: NDP: global unicast address on non-6LBR nodes disappears after a while: Several issues
    4364  (also see #5760) lead to a global unicast address effectively being banned from the network
    4365  (disappears from neighbor cache, is not added again)
    4366  #5467: ipv6 address vanishes when ARO (wrongly) indicates DUP caused by outdated ncache at router
    4367  #5539: Border Router: packet not forwarded from ethos to interface 6
    4368  #5790: ND: Lost of Global IPV6 on node after sending lot of UDP frame from BR
    4369 
    4370  Timer related issues
    4371  --------------------
    4372  #5338: xtimer: xtimer_now() not ISR safe for non-32-bit platforms.
    4373  #6052: tests: xtimer_drift gets stuck: xtimer_drift application freezes after ~30-200 seconds
    4374  #6502: cpu/stm32l1: RTC broken
    4375  #7114: xtimer: add's items to the wrong list if the timer overflows between _xtimer_now() and irq_disable()
    4376 
    4377  native related issues
    4378  ---------------------
    4379  #495: native not float safe: When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either
    4380  the stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    4381  #2175: ubjson: valgind registers "Invalid write of size 4" in unittests
    4382  #5796: native: tlsf: early malloc will lead to a crash: TLSF needs pools to be initialized (which is
    4383  currently expected to be done in an application). If a malloc is needed before an application's
    4384  main started (e.g. driver initialization) the node can crash, since no pool is allocated yet.
    4385  #6145: native: system reboots on SIGTRAP
    4386  #6442: cpu/native: timer interrupt does not yield thread
    4387  #7206: native: race-condition in IPC
    4388 
    4389  other platform related issues
    4390  -----------------------------
    4391  #1891: newlib-nano: Printf formatting does not work properly for some numeric types: PRI[uxdi]64,
    4392  PRI[uxdi]8 and float are not parsed in newlib-nano
    4393  #2143: unittests: tests-core doesn't compile for all platforms: GCC build-ins were used in the
    4394  unittests which are not available with msp430-gcc
    4395  #2300: qemu unittest fails because of a page fault
    4396  #4512: pkg: tests: RELIC unittests fail on iotlab-m3
    4397  #4560: make: clang is more pedantic than gcc oonf_api is not building with clang (partly fixed by #4593)
    4398  #4822: kw2xrf: packet loss when packets get fragmented
    4399  #4876: at86rf2xx: Simultaneous use of different transceiver types is not supported
    4400  #4954: chronos: compiling with -O0 breaks
    4401  #4866: not all GPIO driver implementations are thread safe: Due to non-atomic operations in the drivers
    4402  some pin configurations might get lost.
    4403  #5009: RIOT is saw-toothing in energy consumption (even when idling)
    4404  #5103: xtimer: weird behavior of tests/xtimer_drift: xtimer_drift randomly jumps a few seconds on nrf52
    4405  #5405: Eratic timings on iotlab-m3 with compression context activated
    4406  #5486: at86rf2xx: lost interrupts
    4407  #5678: at86rf2xx: failed assertion in _isr
    4408  #5944: msp430: ipv6_hdr unittests fail
    4409  #5848: arduino: Race condition in sys/arduino/Makefile.include
    4410  #6018: nRF52 gnrc 6lowpan ble memory leak
    4411  #6261: SAMD21 TC3 & TC4 issue when using TCC2
    4412  #6379: nrf52dk/nordic_soft_device: not working anymore
    4413  #6437: periph/spi: Leftovers from SPI rework
    4414  #6526: atmega based boards freeze when main thread is over
    4415  #6836: Issuing a reboot on ATmega328p makes the board loop-reboot
    4416  #7347: xtimer_usleep stuck for small values on nucleo-l1
    4417  #7753: pic32-wifire: race-condition when linking in concurrent build
    4418  #7846: stm32f1: I2C read functions return bogus values with unconnected devices
    4419 
    4420  other issues
    4421  ------------
    4422  #1263: TLSF implementation contains (a) read-before-write error(s).
    4423  #3256: make: Setting constants on compile time doesn't really set them everywhere
    4424  #3366: periph/i2c: handle NACK
    4425  #4488: Making the newlib thread-safe: When calling puts/printf after thread_create(), the CPU hangs
    4426  for DMA enabled uart drivers.
    4427  #5561: C++11 extensions in header files
    4428  #5776: make: Predefining CFLAGS are parsed weirdly
    4429  #5863: OSX + SAMR21-xpro: shell cannot handle command inputs larger than 64 chars
    4430  #5962: Makefile: UNDEF variable is not working as documented

    4472 # Release 2017.07 {#release-2017-07}
    4473 
    4474  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    4475  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    4476  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit microcontrollers, 16-bit
    4477  microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    4478 
    4479  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    4480  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    4481  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    4482 
    4483  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    4484  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    4485  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    4486  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    4487 
    4488  About this release:
    4489  ===================
    4490  This release provides fixes, code cleanup and improved documentation, as well as
    4491  enhancements.
    4492  New features brought by this release include:
    4493  * CAN support (Controller Area Network)
    4494  * Support for CoAP OBSERVE requests
    4495  * Basic Thread stack support (initial support for OpenThread)
    4496  * radio duty cycling with LwMAC protocol
    4497  * LoRa radio drivers supporting Semtech hardware
    4498 
    4499  About 230 pull requests with about 442 commits have been merged since the last
    4500  release and about 13 issues have been solved. 45 people contributed with code
    4501  in 56 days. 1395 files have been touched with 211720 insertions and 65729 deletions.

    4612 # Release 2017.04 {#release-2017-04}
    4613 
    4614  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time
    4615  capabilities and comes with support for a range of devices that are typically
    4616  found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit microcontrollers, 16-bit
    4617  microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    4618 
    4619  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft
    4620  real-time capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API
    4621  access, independent of the underlying hardware (with partial POSIX compliance).
    4622 
    4623  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is
    4624  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    4625  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    4626  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.

    4628  About this release:
    4629  ===================
    4630  This release provides a lot of new features, fixes and enhancements. Among
    4631  these has been a huge cleanup regarding cppcheck and documentation, and we're
    4632  pleased to announce that all remaining doxygen and cppcheck warnings have been
    4633  fixed. We're also proud to present a Virtual File System layer and integration
    4634  of the SPIFFS file system. A lot of work has gone into support for
    4635  STMicroelectronics's Nucleo family, with RIOT now supporting 28 (up from 13)
    4636  Nucleo boards. And as always, there was a lot of under-the-hood cleanup, bug
    4637  fixing and documentation work.
    4638

    4641  716950 insertions and 492623 deletions.

    4726 # Release 2017.01 {#release-2017-01}
    4727 
    4728  RIOT is a multi-threading operating system which enables soft real-time capabilities and comes with
    4729  support for a range of devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit microcontrollers,
    4730  16-bit microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    4731 
    4732  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, soft real-time capabilities,
    4733  small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access, independent of the underlying hardware
    4734  (with partial POSIX compliance).
    4735 
    4736  RIOT is developed by an international open-source community which is independent of specific vendors
    4737  (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1),
    4738  which allows indirect business models around the free open-source software platform provided by RIOT.
    4739 
    4740  About this release:
    4741  ===================
    4742  This release provides a lot of new features, fixes and enhancements. Among others these features
    4743  contain an initial - still experimental - TCP implementation based on the GNRC network stack, support
    4744  for reading from and writing to SD cards, a new power management architecture as well additional third
    4745  party packages such as TweetNaCl, a cryptographic library, and Heatshrink a data compression library
    4746  optimized for embedded real-time systems.
    4747  We added support for new platforms including the Calliope mini, Maple mini, and a couple of STMs
    4748  Nucleo boards. Device support was extended by several new drivers, e.g., for NXP PN532 NFC, Microchip
    4749  MRF24J40 802.15.4 radio (experimental), or Bosch BME280 pressure/humidity/temperature sensor.
    4750  We completely refactored the SPI interface, allowing for internally handled hardware or software chip
    4751  select lines and shared bus usage for multiple devices with different SPI configurations.
    4752 
    4753  About 278 pull requests with about 606 commits have been merged since the last release and about 84
    4754  issues have been solved. 44 people contributed with code in 87 days. 2230 files have been touched with
    4755  220275 insertions and 159840 deletions.
    4756 
    4757  Notations used below:

    4845  #4874: Using single RSSI_BASE_VALUE for all Atmel radios
    4846  #5034: gnrc_networking: offers txtsnd, does not print received packets
    4847  #5083: AVR8: Reboots after `return 0;`
    4848  #5719: cc2538: rf driver doesn't handle large packets
    4849  #5954: nRF52 uart_write gets stuck
    4850  #6036: tinydtls: DTLS randomly missing functions
    4851  #6037: pkg/nanocoap: native build fails on macOS
    4852  #6358: arduino uno : xtimer accuracy problem
    4853 
    4854  Known Issues
    4855  ============
    4856  Networking related issues
    4857  -------------------------
    4858  #3075: nhdp: unnecessary microsecond precision: NHDP works with timer values of microsecond precision
    4859  which is not required. Changing to lower precision would save some memory.
    4860  #4048: potential racey memory leak: According to the packet buffer stats, flood-pinging a multicast
    4861  destination may lead to a memory leak due to a race condition. However, it seems to be a rare
    4862  case and a completely filled up packet buffer was not observed.
    4863  #5016: gnrc_rpl: Rejoining RPL instance as root after reboot messes up routing
    4864  #5230: gnrc ipv6: multicast packets are not dispatched to the upper layers
    4865  #5656: Possible Weakness with locking in the GNRC network stack: For some operations mutexes to the
    4866  network interfaces need to get unlocked in the current implementation to not get deadlocked.
    4867  Recursive mutexes as provided in #5731 might help to solve this problem.
    4868  #5748: gnrc: nodes crashing with too small packet buffer: A packet buffer of size ~512 B might lead
    4869  to crashes. The issue describes this for several hundret nodes, but agressive flooding with
    4870  just two nodes was also shown to lead to this problem.
    4871  #5858: gnrc: 6lo: potential problem with reassembly of fragments: If one frame gets lost the reassembly
    4872  state machine might get out of sync
    4873  #6123: gnrc: crash with (excessive) traffic
    4874 
    4875  NDP is not working properly
    4876  ---------------------------
    4877  #4499: handle of l2src_len in gnrc_ndp_rtr_sol_handle: Reception of a router solicitation might lead
    4878  to invalid zero-length link-layer addresses in neighbor cache.
    4879  #5005: ndp: router advertisement sent with global address: Under some circumstances a router might
    4880  send RAs with GUAs. While they are ignored on receive (as RFC-4861 specifies), RAs should have
    4881  link-local addresses and not even be send out this way.
    4882  #5122: NDP: global unicast address on non-6LBR nodes disappears after a while: Several issues
    4883  (also see #5760) lead to a global unicast address effectively being banned from the network
    4884  (disappears from neighbor cache, is not added again)
    4885  #5467: ipv6 address vanishes when ARO (wrongly) indicates DUP caused by outdated ncache at router
    4886  #5539: Border Router: packet not forwarded from ethos to interface 6
    4887  #5790: ND: Lost of Global IPV6 on node after sending lot of UDP frame from BR
    4888 
    4889  Timer related issues
    4890  --------------------
    4891  #4841: xtimer: timer already in the list: Under some conditions an xtimer can end up twice in the
    4892  internal list of the xtimer module
    4893  #4902: xtimer: xtimer_set: xtimer_set does not handle integer overflows well
    4894  #5338: xtimer: xtimer_now() not ISR safe for non-32-bit platforms.
    4895  #5928: xtimer: usage in board_init() crashes: some boards use the xtimer in there board_init()
    4896  function. The xtimer is however first initialized in the auto_init module which is executed
    4897  after board_init()
    4898  #6052: tests: xtimer_drift gets stuck: xtimer_drift application freezes after ~30-200 seconds
    4899  #6331: RTC alarm triggered with 1s delay
    4900  #6419: cpu/cc2538: timer broken
    4901  #6427: xtimer: infinite loop with xtimer_mutex_lock_timeout
    4902  #6502: cpu/stm32l1: RTC broken
    4903  #6542: boards/nucle-f0xx: misconfigured timer configuration (fix in #6494)
    4904 
    4905  native related issues
    4906  ---------------------
    4907  #495: native not float safe: When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either
    4908  the stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    4909  #2175: ubjson: valgind registers "Invalid write of size 4" in unittests
    4910  #4590: pkg: building relic with clang fails.
    4911  #5796: native: tlsf: early malloc will lead to a crash: TLSF needs pools to be initialized (which is
    4912  currently expected to be done in an application). If a malloc is needed before an application's
    4913  main started (e.g. driver initialization) the node can crash, since no pool is allocated yet.
    4914  #6145: native: system reboots on SIGTRAP
    4915  #6442: cpu/native: timer interrupt does not yield thread
    4916 
    4917  other platform related issues
    4918  -----------------------------
    4919  #1891: newlib-nano: Printf formatting does not work properly for some numeric types: PRI[uxdi]64,
    4920  PRI[uxdi]8 and float are not parsed in newlib-nano
    4921  #2006: cpu/nrf51822: timer callback may be fired too early
    4922  #2143: unittests: tests-core doesn't compile for all platforms: GCC build-ins were used in the
    4923  unittests which are not available with msp430-gcc
    4924  #2300: qemu unittest fails because of a page fault
    4925  #4512: pkg: tests: RELIC unittests fail on iotlab-m3
    4926  #4560: make: clang is more pedantic than gcc oonf_api is not building with clang (partly fixed by #4593)
    4927  #4694: drivers/lm75a: does not build
    4928  #4822: kw2xrf: packet loss when packets get fragmented
    4929  #4876: at86rf2xx: Simultaneous use of different transceiver types is not supported
    4930  #4954: chronos: compiling with -O0 breaks
    4931  #4866: not all GPIO driver implementations are thread safe: Due to non-atomic operations in the drivers
    4932  some pin configurations might get lost.
    4933  #5009: RIOT is saw-toothing in energy consumption (even when idling)
    4934  #5103: xtimer: weird behavior of tests/xtimer_drift: xtimer_drift randomly jumps a few seconds on nrf52
    4935  #5361: cpu/cc26x0: timer broken
    4936  #5405: Eratic timings on iotlab-m3 with compression context activated
    4937  #5460: cpu/samd21: i2c timing with compiler optimization
    4938  #5486: at86rf2xx: lost interrupts
    4939  #5489: cpu/lpc11u34: ADC broken
    4940  #5678: at86rf2xx: failed assertion in _isr
    4941  #5799: kw2x: 15.4 duplicate transmits
    4942  #5944: msp430: ipv6_hdr unittests fail
    4943  #5848: arduino: Race condition in sys/arduino/Makefile.include
    4944  #6018: nRF52 gnrc 6lowpan ble memory leak
    4945  #6261: SAMD21 TC3 & TC4 issue when using TCC2
    4946  #6379: nrf52dk/nordic_soft_device: not working anymore
    4947  #6437: periph/spi: Leftovers from SPI rework
    4948  #6501: boards/nucleo: Pin usage collision (SPI clk vs. LED0)
    4949  #6526: atmega based boards freeze when main thread is over
    4950 
    4951  other issues
    4952  ------------
    4953  #1263: TLSF implementation contains (a) read-before-write error(s).
    4954  #3256: make: Setting constants on compile time doesn't really set them everywhere
    4955  #3366: periph/i2c: handle NACK
    4956  #4488: Making the newlib thread-safe: When calling puts/printf after thread_create(), the CPU hangs
    4957  for DMA enabled uart drivers.
    4958  #4866: periph: GPIO drivers are not thread safe
    4959  #5128: make: buildtest breaks when exporting FEATURES_PROVIDED var

    5004 # Release 2016.10 {#release-2016-10}
    5005 
    5006  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    5007  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit
    5008  microcontrollers, 16-bit microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    5009 
    5010  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    5011  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    5012  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    5013  compliance).
    5014 
    5015  RIOT is developed by an international open source community which is
    5016  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community) and is
    5017  licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows indirect
    5018  business models around the free open-source software platform provided by
    5019  RIOT.
    5020 
    5021  About this release:
    5022  ===================
    5023  This release provides a lot of new features as well as it fixes several major
    5024  bugs. Among these new features are the new simplified network socket API
    5025  called sock, the GNRC specific CoAP implementation gcoap and several new
    5026  packages: TinyDTLS, the Aversive++ microcontroller library for robotics, the
    5027  u8g2 graphic library, and nanocoap.
    5028  Using the new sock API an implementation of the Simple Time Network Protocol
    5029  (SNTP) was also introduced, allowing for time synchronization between nodes.
    5030  New platforms include the Arduino Uno, the Arduino Duemilanove, the Arduino
    5031  Zero, SODAQ Autonomo, and the Zolertia remote (rev. B).
    5032  The most significant bug fix was done in native which led to a significantly
    5033  more robust handling of ISRs and now allows for at least 1,000 native
    5034  instances running stably on one machine.
    5035 
    5036  About 263 pull requests with about 398 commits have been merged since the last
    5037  release and about 42 issues have been solved. 37 people contributed with code
    5038  in 100 days. 1006 files have been touched with 166500 insertions and 26926
    5039  deletions.
    5040 
    5041  Notations used below:
    5042  =====================
    5043  + means new feature/item
    5044  * means modified feature/item
    5045  - means removed feature/item
    5046 
    5047  New features and changes
    5048  ========================
    5049  General
    5050  -------
    5051  * Verbose behavior for assert() macro
    5052 
    5053  Core
    5054  ----
    5055  + MPU support for Cortex-M
    5056 
    5057  API changes
    5058  -----------
    5059  + Socket-like sock API (replacing conn)
    5060  * netdev: Add Testmodes and CCA modes
    5061  * IEEE 802.15.4: clean-up Intra-PAN behavior
    5062  * IEEE 802.15.4: centralize default values
    5063  * gnrc_pktbuf: allow for 0-sized snips
    5064  + gnrc_netapi: mbox and arbitrary callback support
    5065 
    5066  System libraries
    5067  ----------------
    5068  No new features or changes
    5069 
    5070  Networking
    5071  ----------
    5072  + Provide sock-port for GNRC
    5073  + gcoap: a GNRC-based CoAP implementation
    5074  + Simple Network Time Protocol (RFC 5905, section 14)
    5075  + Priority Queue for packet snips
    5076  + IPv4 header definitions
    5077 
    5078  Packages
    5079  --------
    5080  + nanocoap: CoAP header parser/builder
    5081  + TinyDTLS: DTLS library
    5082  + tiny-asn1: asn.1/der decoder
    5083  + Aversive++ microcontroller programming library
    5084  + u8g2 graphic library
    5085 
    5086  Platforms
    5087  ---------
    5088  + Support for stm32f2xx MCU family
    5089  + Low power modes for samd21 CPUs
    5090  + More Arduino-based platforms:
    5091  + Arduino Uno
    5092  + Arduino Duemilanove
    5093  + Arduino Zero
    5094  + More boards of ST's Nucleo platforms:
    5095  + ST Nucleo F030 board support
    5096  + ST Nucleo F070 board support
    5097  + ST Nucleo F446 board support
    5098  + SODAQ Automono
    5099  + Zolertia remote rev. B
    5100 
    5101  Drivers
    5102  -------
    5103  + W5100 Ethernet device
    5104  + Atmel IO1 Xplained extension
    5105  + LPD8808 LED strips
    5106  * at86rf2xx: provide capability to access the RND_VALUE random value register
    5107 
    5108  Build System
    5109  ------------
    5110  + static-tests build target for easy local execution of CI's static tests
    5111 
    5112  Other
    5113  -----
    5114  + Provide Arduino API to Nucleo boards
    5115  + Packer configuration file to build vagrant boxes
    5116  + CC2650STK Debugger Support
    5117  + ethos: add Ethos over TCP support

    5127  Known Issues
    5128  ============
    5129  Networking related issues
    5130  -------------------------
    5131  #3075: nhdp: unnecessary microsecond precision: NHDP works with timer values
    5132  of microsecond precision which is not required. Changing to lower
    5133  precision would save some memory.
    5134  #4048: potential racey memory leak: According to the packet buffer stats,
    5135  flood-pinging a multicast destination may lead to a memory leak due to
    5136  a race condition. However, it seems to be a rare case and a completely
    5137  filled up packet buffer was not observed.
    5138  #4388: POSIX sockets: open socket is bound to a specific thread: This was an
    5139  inherit problem of the conn API under GNRC. Since the POSIX sockets are
    5140  still based on conn for this release, this issue persists
    5141  #4527: gnrc_ipv6: Multicast is not forwarded if routing node listens to the
    5142  address (might still be fixable for release, see #5729, #5230: gnrc
    5143  ipv6: multicast packets are not dispatched to the upper layers)
    5144  #5016: gnrc_rpl: Rejoining RPL instance as root after reboot messes up routing
    5145  #5055: cpuid: multiple radios will get same EUI-64 Nodes with multiple
    5146  interfaces might get the same EUI-64 for them since they are generated
    5147  from the same CPU ID.
    5148  #5656: Possible Weakness with locking in the GNRC network stack: For some
    5149  operations mutexes to the network interfaces need to get unlocked in
    5150  the current implementation to not get deadlocked. Recursive mutexes as
    5151  provided in #5731 might help to solve this problem.
    5152  #5748: gnrc: nodes crashing with too small packet buffer: A packet buffer of
    5153  size ~512 B might lead to crashes. The issue describes this for several
    5154  hundret nodes, but agressive flooding with just two nodes was also
    5155  shown to lead to this problem.
    5156  #5858: gnrc: 6lo: potential problem with reassembly of fragments: If one frame
    5157  gets lost the reassembly state machine might get out of sync
    5158 
    5159  ### NDP is not working properly
    5160  #4499: handle of l2src_len in gnrc_ndp_rtr_sol_handle: Reception of a router
    5161  solicitation might lead to invalid zero-length link-layer addresses in
    5162  neighbor cache.
    5163  #5005: ndp: router advertisement sent with global address: Under some
    5164  circumstances a router might send RAs with GUAs. While they are ignored
    5165  on receive (as RFC 4861 specifies), RAs should have link-local
    5166  addresses and not even be send out this way.
    5167  #5122: NDP: global unicast address on non-6LBR nodes disappears after a while:
    5168  Several issues (also see #5760) lead to a global unicast address
    5169  effectively being banned from the network (disappears from neighbor
    5170  cache, is not added again)
    5171  #5467: ipv6 address vanishes when ARO (wrongly) indicates DUP caused by
    5172  outdated ncache at router
    5173  #5539: Border Router: packet not forwarded from ethos to interface 6
    5174  #5790: ND: Lost of Global IPV6 on node after sending lot of UDP frame from BR
    5175 
    5176  Timer related issues
    5177  --------------------
    5178  #4841: xtimer: timer already in the list: Under some conditions an xtimer can
    5179  end up twice in the internal list of the xtimer module
    5180  #4902: xtimer: xtimer_set: xtimer_set does not handle integer overflows well
    5181  #5338: xtimer: xtimer_now() not ISR safe for non-32-bit platforms.
    5182  #5928: xtimer: usage in board_init() crashes: some boards use the xtimer in
    5183  there board_init() function. The xtimer is however first initialized in

    5185  #6052: tests: xtimer_drift gets stuck: xtimer_drift application freezes after
    5186  ~30-200 seconds
    5187 
    5188  native related issues
    5189  ---------------------
    5190  #495: native not float safe: When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context
    5191  switch occurs, either the stack gets corrupted or a floating point
    5192  exception occurs.
    5193  #2175: ubjson: valgind registers "Invalid write of size 4" in unittests
    5194  #4590: pkg: building relic with clang fails.
    5195  #5796: native: tlsf: early malloc will lead to a crash: TLSF needs pools to be
    5196  initialized (which is currently expected to be done in an application).
    5197  If a malloc is needed before an application's main started (e.g. driver
    5198  initialization) the node can crash, since no pool is allocated yet.
    5199

    5296 # Release 2016.07 {#release-2016-07}
    5297 
    5298  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    5299  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit
    5300  microcontrollers, 16-bit microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    5301 
    5302  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    5303  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    5304  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    5305  compliance).
    5306 
    5307  RIOT is developed by an international open source community which is
    5308  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community)
    5309  and is licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows
    5310  indirect business models around the free open-source software platform
    5311  provided by RIOT.
    5312 
    5313  About this release:

    5315  This release was focused primarily on fixing bugs, but also adds two new
    5316  supported radio transceivers: CC2420 and CC2538.
    5317  This new radio support allows to new interoperability tests with other OS,
    5318  allowing code size comparison and overall network performance for
    5319  platforms based on these radios.

    5387  Fixed Issues from the last release
    5388  ==================================
    5389  #3824: native: gnrc: hardcore pinging crashes.
    5390  #4583: cpp11: clang doesn't allow mutex_t to be used with constexpr All
    5391  cpp11-* tests fail with clang.
    5392  #5388: gnrc_sixlowpan_iphc_nhc: receiving NHC compressed UDP
    5393  packets hits assert in IPv6 (Fixed by #5281).
    5394 
    5395  Known Issues
    5396  ==========
    5397  #3075: nhdp: unnecessary microsecond precision NHDP works with timer
    5398  values of microsecond precision which is not required. Changing to lower
    5399  precision would save some memory.
    5400  #3086: Max. packet length for AT86RF2XX
    5401  #4048: potential racey memory leak According to the packet buffer stats,
    5402  flood-pinging a multicast destination may lead to a memory leak due to a
    5403  race condition. However, it seems to be a rare case and a completely filled
    5404  up packet buffer was not observed.
    5405  #5005: ndp: router advertisement sent with global address Under some
    5406  circumstances a router might send RAs with GUAs. While they are ignored
    5407  on receive (as RFC 4861 specifies), RAs should have link-local addresses
    5408  and not even be send out this way.
    5409  #5007: gnrc icmpv6: Ping reply goes out the wrong interface
    5410  #5055: cpuid: multiple radios will get same EUI-64 Nodes with multiple
    5411  interfaces might get the same EUI-64 for them since they are generated from
    5412  the same CPU ID.
    5413  #5230: gnrc ipv6: multicast packets are not dispatched to the upper layers.
    5414  (Fix exists, but was postponed)
    5415  #5390: pkg: OpenWSN does not compile This package still uses deprecated
    5416  modules and was not tested for a long time.
    5417 
    5418  native related issues
    5419  ---------------------
    5420  #495: native not float safe When the FPU is used when an asynchronous
    5421  context switch occurs, either the stack gets corrupted or a floating point
    5422  exception occurs.
    5423  #534: native debugging on osx fails Using valgrind or gdb with a nativenet
    5424  target in OSX leads to "the network" being stuck (gdb) or the whole process
    5425  being stuck (valgrind).
    5426  #334: nativenet crashes when hammered Flood-pinging a native instance
    5427  from more than one host (either multiple threads on the host system or multiple
    5428  other native instances), leads to a SEGFAULT.
    5429  #2071; WIP: native: overdue fixes
    5430  #4590: pkg: building relic with clang fails.
    5431  #5432: native: valgrind fails
    5432 
    5433  other platform related issues
    5434  -----------------------------
    5435  #4560: make: clang is more pedantic than gcc oonf_api is not building with
    5436  clang.
    5437  (Partly solved by #4593)
    5438  #4866: not all GPIO driver implementations are thread safe Due to non-atomic
    5439  operations in the drivers some pin configurations might get lost.
    5440  #5486: at86rf2xx: lost interrupts
    5441 
    5442  other issues
    5443  ------------
    5444  #1263: TLSF implementation contains (a) read-before-write error(s).
    5445  #2761: core: define default flags If a thread is created without the
    5446  corresponding flag (CREATE_STACKTEST), the ps command will yield wrong
    5447  numbers for the stack usage.
    5448  #2927: core: Automatically select the lowest possible LPM mode Not all
    5449  available low power modes (LPMs) are implemented for each platform and the
    5450  concept of how the LPM is chosen needs some reconsideration.
    5451  #2967: Makefile.features: location is not relevant for all features Provided
    5452  features for the build system should be split up into a board and cpu specific part
    5453  #4488: Making the newlib thread-safe When calling puts/printf after
    5454  thread_create(), the CPU hangs for DMA enabled uart drivers.
    5455  #4841: xtimer: timer already in the list Under some conditions an xtimer can end
    5456  up twice in the internal list of the xtimer module.
    5457  #5338: xtimer: xtimer_now() not ISR safe For non-32-bit platforms.

    5496 # Release 2016.04 {#release-2016-04}
    5497 
    5498  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    5499  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit
    5500  microcontrollers, 16-bit microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    5501 
    5502  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    5503  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    5504  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    5505  compliance).
    5506 
    5507  RIOT is developed by an international open source community which is
    5508  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community)
    5509  and is licensed with a non-viral copyleft license (LGPLv2.1), which allows
    5510  indirect business models around the free open-source software platform
    5511  provided by RIOT.
    5512 
    5513  About this release:
    5514  ===================
    5515  This release adds support for two additional network stacks: lwIP and emb6.
    5516  A bunch of additional protocols are now available, P2P-RPL in the GNRC
    5517  network stack, Ethernet-over-Serial (ethos). Murdock, the new, blazing fast
    5518  RIOT CI is now available to significantly speed up code merging procedures.
    5519 
    5520  This release also adds support for a number of new boards and sensors and a new
    5521  tool for automated border router setup is now provided which greatly simplifies
    5522  that setup for newbies as well as for old-timers. Last but not least: this
    5523  release includes a number of bug fixes, mostly about stabilizing and enhancing
    5524  the networking capabilities of RIOT.
    5525 
    5526  About 470 pull requests with about 1196 commits have been merged since the last
    5527  release and 127 additional issues have been solved. 55 people contributed code
    5528  in 124 days. 1521 files have been touched with ~91700 insertions and ~42200
    5529  deletions.
    5530 
    5531  Notations used below:
    5532  =====================
    5533  + means new feature/item
    5534  * means modified feature/item
    5535  - means removed feature/item
    5536 
    5537  New features and changes
    5538  ========================
    5539  General
    5540  ----------
    5541  + added Makefile support for creating a "binary distribution", making it easier to create closed source applications while still complying to LGPL
    5542 
    5543  Testing
    5544  ---
    5545  + Murdock, the new RIOT CI
    5546  + unified pexpect code
    5547  + added various new unittests and test applications
    5548 
    5549  Core
    5550  ----
    5551  + added thread flags, a new method to signal events in an efficient and thread safe manner
    5552  + messaging is now compile-time optional, shaving off some bytes off each thread's state struct for projects not requiring it
    5553  + new, simpler list implementation increases mutex and msg performance
    5554 
    5555  Network Stack
    5556  ---
    5557  + P2P-RPL (RFC6997)
    5558  + netdev_test: test framework for users of the netdev API
    5559 
    5560  Packages
    5561  ---
    5562  + emb6 network stack
    5563  + jsmn (minimal JSON parser)
    5564  + lwIP network stack
    5565  + unified and streamlined git package source handling
    5566  + added support for caching git repositories
    5567 
    5568  Platforms
    5569  ---
    5570  + reworked existing peripheral drivers and added SPI driver for arduino-mega2560
    5571  + added support for nRF52dk
    5572  + added support for nucleo-f072 and nucleo-f103
    5573  + unified LED macros for all boards
    5574 
    5575  Drivers
    5576  ---
    5577  + ethos "ethernet over serial" driver, enabling shared uart + network communication over one serial connection
    5578  + RHOM BH1750FVI ambient light sensor
    5579  + ST LIS3MDL three-axis magnetic sensor
    5580  + Silicon Labs Si70xx low-power temperature + humidity sensor
    5581  + simplified GPIO driver interface
    5582  + AES encryption for xbee radio driver
    5583  + added ADC mapping to SAUL
    5584 
    5585  Sytem libraries
    5586  ---
    5587  - vtimer support was dropped completely and removed
    5588 
    5589  Build System
    5590  ---
    5591  + made build system safe for concurrent building of multiple applications
    5592  + desvirt integration into the RIOT build system
    5593 
    5594  Other
    5595  ---
    5596  - simplified border router setup tool (single UART and automation script)
    5597 
    5598  API changes
    5599  ---
    5600  * at86rf2xx was moved from gnrc_netdev to the netdev API
    5601  * genrand_* -> random_*
    5602  * xtimer_remove() no longer returns whether a timer was actually removed
    5603  * disableIRQ(), enableIRQ(), restoreIRQ(), inISR() -> irq_disable(), irq_enable(), irq_restore(), irq_is_in()
    5604  * renamed periph/random to periph/hwrng
    5605 
    5606  Fixed Issues from the last release
    5607  ==================================
    5608  * #3109: periph/random: random_read should return unsigned int
    5609  * #3970: RPL: Advertise DODAG only over the assigned interface
    5610  * #4462: IPHC/NHC broken between Linux and a RIOT node with a RIOT-based border router in between.
    5611  * #4608: tests/xtimer_usleep_until: unstable behaviour
    5612 
    5613  Known Issues
    5614  ==========
    5615  ----------------------
    5616  * #3075: nhdp: unnecessary microsecond precision
    5617  NHDP works with timer values of microsecond precision which is not required. Changing
    5618  to lower precision would save some memory.
    5619  * #3086: Max. packet length for AT86RF2XX
    5620  The size of the link-layer header is not dynamically calculated, but instead the maximum
    5621  size is always assumed.
    5622  * #4048: potential racey memory leak
    5623  According to the packet buffer stats, flood-pinging a multicast destination may lead to a
    5624  memory leak due to a race condition. However, it seems to be a rare case and a
    5625  completely filled up packet buffer was not observed.
    5626  * #5005: ndp: router advertisement sent with global address
    5627  Under some circumstances a router might send RAs with GUAs. While they are ignored
    5628  on receive (as RFC 4861 specifies), RAs should have link-local addresses and not even
    5629  be send out this way.
    5630  * #5007: gnrc icmpv6: Ping reply goes out the wrong interface
    5631  * #5055: cpuid: multiple radios will get same EUI-64
    5632  Nodes with multiple interfaces might get the same EUI-64 for them since they are generated
    5633  from the same CPU ID
    5634  * #5230: gnrc ipv6: multicast packets are not dispatched to the upper layers
    5635  * #5388: gnrc_sixlowpan_iphc_nhc: receiving NHC compressed UDP packets hits assert in IPv6
    5636  Fix already provided in #5281, but did not made it into the release due to its complexity
    5637  * #5390: pkg: OpenWSN does not compile
    5638  This package still uses deprecated modules and was not tested for a long time
    5639 
    5640  native related issues
    5641  ---------------------
    5642  * #495: native not float safe
    5643  When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either the
    5644  stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    5645  * #534: native debugging on osx fails
    5646  Using valgrind or gdb with a nativenet target in OSX leads to "the network"
    5647  being stuck (gdb) or the whole process being stuck (valgrind).
    5648  * #3341 and #3824: nativenet crashes when hammered
    5649  Flood-pinging a native instance from more than one host (either multiple threads on the
    5650  host system or multiple other native instances), leads to a SEGFAULT
    5651 
    5652  other platform related issues
    5653  -----------------------------
    5654  * #4560: make: clang is more pedantic than gcc
    5655  oonf_api is not building with clang.
    5656  * #4583: cpp11: clang doesn't allow `mutex_t` to be used with `constexpr`
    5657  All cpp11-* tests fail with clang.
    5658  * #4866: not all GPIO driver implementations are thread safe
    5659  Due to non-atomic operations in the drivers some pin configurations might get lost
    5660 
    5661  other issues
    5662  ------------
    5663  * #1263: TLSF implementation contains (a) read-before-write error(s)
    5664  * #2761: core: define default flags
    5665  If a thread is created without the corresponding flag (CREATE_STACKTEST),
    5666  the ps command will yield wrong numbers for the stack usage
    5667  * #2927: core: Automatically select the lowest possible LPM mode
    5668  Not all available low power modes (LPMs) are implemented for each platform and the
    5669  concept of how the LPM is chosen needs some reconsideration
    5670  * #2967: Makefile.features: location is not relevant for all features
    5671  Provided features for the build system should be split up into a board and cpu specific
    5672  part
    5673  * #4488: Making the newlib thread-safe
    5674  When calling puts/printf after thread_create(), the CPU hangs for DMA enabled uart drivers.
    5675  * #4841: xtimer: timer already in the list
    5676  Under some conditions an xtimer can end up twice in the internal list of the xtimer module.
    5677  * #5338: xtimer: xtimer_now() not ISR safe
    5678  For non-32-bit platforms
    5679
