    5717 # Release 2015.12 {#release-2015-12}
    5718 
    5719  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    5720  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: 8-bit
    5721  microcontrollers, 16-bit microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit processors.
    5722 
    5723  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    5724  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    5725  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    5726  compliance).
    5727 
    5728  RIOT is developed by an international open source community which is
    5729  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community).
    5730 
    5731  About this release:
    5732  ===================
    5733  This release is mostly a clean-up and bug-fixing release. Besides that, it introduces SAUL,
    5734  the [S]ensor [A]ctuator [U]ber [L]ayer, which offers a unified API to interact with all
    5735  different types of sensors and actuators on RIOT supported hardware. Furthermore, it re-enables
    5736  the support for ICN by integrating CCN-Lite as a package. A lot of new overall documentation was
    5737  added and existing documentation was improved (http://riot-os.org/api/). In addition,
    5738  a Vagrant (https://www.vagrantup.com/) configuration file was added to the RIOT repository in
    5739  order to create reproducible and portable environments that contain all necessary toolchains.
    5740 
    5741  About 222 pull requests with about 631 commits have been merged since the last release and 48
    5742  additional issues have been solved. 37 people contributed code in 102 days. 980 files have been
    5743  touched with ~59779 insertions and ~12115 deletions.
    5744 
    5745  Notations used below:
    5746  =====================

    5748  * means modified feature/item
    5749  - means removed feature/item

    5835  Fixed Issues from the last release
    5836  ==================================
    5837 
    5838  #2724: Add support for serial number passing to CMSIS boards, document it
    5839  Documentation about how to discover and set the serial number of CMSIS-DAP chips is missing
    5840  #3201: Odd length packet snips cause invalid check sum
    5841  If an odd length packet snip occurs in a packet and is not the last snip
    5842  (in the order the packet is supposed to be, not in the list's order)
    5843  in a packet it will generate a wrong check sum.

    5845  Known Issues

    5848  network related issues
    5849  ----------------------
    5850  #3075: nhdp: unnecessary microsecond precision
    5851  NHDP works with timer values of microsecond precision which is not required. Changing
    5852  to lower precision would save some memory.
    5853  #3086: Max. packet length for AT86RF2XX
    5854  The size of the link-layer header is not dynamically calculated, but instead the maximum
    5855  size is always assumed.
    5856  #3970: RPL: Advertise DODAG only over the assigned interface
    5857  gnrc_rpl seems to multicast DIOs over all interfaces, though gnrc_rpl_init expects an
    5858  interface as parameter and sets the RPL-nodes multicast address only for that interface.
    5859  #4048: potential racey memory leak
    5860  According to the packet buffer stats, flood-pinging a multicast destination may lead to a
    5861  memory leak due to a race condition. However, it seems to be a rare case and a
    5862  completely filled up packet buffer was not observed.
    5863  #4462: IPHC/NHC broken between Linux and a RIOT node with a RIOT-based border router in between.
    5864 
    5865  native related issues
    5866  ---------------------
    5867  #495: native not float safe
    5868  When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either the
    5869  stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    5870  #534: native debugging on osx fails
    5871  Using valgrind or gdb with a nativenet target in OSX leads to "the network"
    5872  being stuck (gdb) or the whole process being stuck (valgrind).
    5873  #3341 and #3824: nativenet crashes when hammered
    5874  Flood-pinging a native instance from more than one host (either multiple threads on the
    5875  host system or multiple other native instances), leads to a SEGFAULT.
    5876  #4608: tests/xtimer_usleep_until: unstable behaviour
    5877  The test starts to output "too large difference" and fails after a random period of time.
    5878 
    5879  other platform related issues
    5880  -----------------------------
    5881  #4560: make: clang is more pedantic than gcc
    5882  oonf_api is not building with clang.
    5883  #4583: cpp11: clang doesn't allow `mutex_t` to be used with `constexpr`
    5884  All cpp11-* tests fail with clang.
    5885 
    5886  other issues
    5887  ------------
    5888  #2761: core: define default flags
    5889  If a thread is created without the corresponding flag (CREATE_STACKTEST),
    5890  the ps command will yield wrong numbers for the stack usage
    5891  #2927: core: Automatically select the lowest possible LPM mode
    5892  Not all available low power modes (LPMs) are implemented for each platform and the
    5893  concept of how the LPM is chosen needs some reconsideration
    5894  #2967: Makefile.features: location is not relevant for all features
    5895  Provided features for the build system should be split up into a board and cpu specific
    5896  part
    5897  #3109: periph/random: random_read should return unsigned int
    5898  The documentation of this function does not match corresponding implementation.
    5899  #4488: Making the newlib thread-safe
    5900  When calling puts/printf after thread_create(), the CPU hangs for DMA enabled uart drivers.
    5901

    5939 # Release 2015.09 {#release-2015-09}
    5940 
    5941  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    5942  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: devices based on
    5943  8-bit microcontrollers, 16-bit microcontrollers and light-weight 32-bit
    5944  processors.
    5945 
    5946  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    5947  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    5948  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    5949  compliance).
    5950 
    5951  RIOT is developed by an international open source community which is
    5952  independent of specific vendors (e.g. similarly to the Linux community).
    5953 
    5954  About this release:
    5955  ============
    5956  This release introduces the GNRC network stack, a completely new, highly
    5957  modularized and configurable IPv6/6LoWPAN stack. It also includes xtimer as a
    5958  new timer subsystem for accurate short- and long-term timers. Moreover,
    5959  peripheral drivers, board, and CPU support has been tidied up and contains
    5960  about 50% less duplication in the build system.
    5961 
    5962  About 580 pull requests with about 2,500 commits have been merged since the
    5963  last release and 120 additional issues have been solved. 62 people contributed
    5964  code in 278 days. 2578 files have been touched with ~320,000 insertions and
    5965  ~134,000 deletions.
    5966 
    5967  Loose notations used below:
    5968  ============
    5969  + means new feature/item
    5970  * means modified feature/item
    5971  - means removed feature/item
    5972 
    5973  New features
    5974  ============
    5975 
    5976  General
    5977  -------
    5978  + complete codebase now compiles with -Werror on all platforms
    5979 
    5980  Device support
    5981  --------------
    5982  + vastly improved hardware abstraction, unified over all devices
    5983  + unified most common code
    5984  * complete refactoring of MSP430 and ARM7 code
    5985 
    5986  Core
    5987  ----
    5988  + new timer subsystem: xtimer
    5989  + extended atomic API by compare-and-swap, increase/decrease and
    5990  set-to-one/set-to-zero functions
    5991  + introduced a more energy-saving assert macro
    5992 
    5993  Network Stack
    5994  -------------
    5995  + RFC compliant gnrc network stack (6LoWPAN, IPv6, UDP, RPL) major refactoring
    5996  + 6LoWPAN ND (including SLAAC)
    5997  + example applications working out of the box (gnrc_networking for the full
    5998  gnrc experience, gnrc_border_router for a 6LoWPAN border router, and default
    5999  for simple link layer connectivity)
    6000  + explicit support for border router
    6001  + auto-init for the network stack
    6002  + introduction of generic interfaces (netdev, netapi)
    6003  + introduction of a protocol-independent FIB
    6004  + introduction of a central packet buffer
    6005  + wireshark-supported protocol ZEP to send IEEE 802.15.4 frames over UDP on
    6006  non-IEEE-802.15.4 devices
    6007  + support for SLIP and link-layers without addresses
    6008  + new low-level driver model
    6009  + new nativenet based directly on ethernet
    6010  + conn: general stack-independent transport layer API
    6011  + POSIX sockets ported for conn
    6012  + NHDP support
    6013 
    6014  Packages
    6015  --------
    6016  + support for microCoAP
    6017  + CMSIS DSP
    6018 
    6019  Supported platforms
    6020  -------------------
    6021  Additional support for the following boards:
    6022  + Zolertia ReMote
    6023  + Atmel SAML21 Xplained Pro (saml21-xpro)
    6024  + ST Nucleo L1
    6025  + ST Nucleo F334
    6026  + ST Nucleo F091
    6027  + Phytec phyWAVE KW22
    6028  + Eistec Mulle
    6029  + Freescale Freedom FRDM-K64F
    6030  + TI Stellaris Launchpad LM4F120
    6031  + LimiFrog V1
    6032  + Silabs EZR32WG
    6033 
    6034  Drivers
    6035  -------
    6036  + various peripheral drivers (ADC, UART, timer, SPI, IC, RTC, RTT, DAC, PWM...)
    6037  + basic NVRAM driver (interface)
    6038 
    6039  Network drivers
    6040  + native ethernet driver
    6041  + ENCx24J600 ethernet driver
    6042 
    6043  Sensors drivers
    6044  + ISL29125 RGB light sensor
    6045  + PDC8544 LCD display
    6046  + INA220 current and power monitor
    6047  + MPU-9150 9-DOF motion sensor
    6048  + LIS3DH accelerometer
    6049  + TMP006 temperature sensor
    6050  + MAG3110 magnetometer
    6051  + MMA8652 accelerometer
    6052  + DHT11/DHT22 temperature-humidity sensor
    6053  + ADT7310 temperature sensor
    6054 
    6055  System libraries
    6056  ----------------
    6057  + MD5
    6058  + Fletcher's checksum
    6059  + Unified Cipher API and Block cipher operation modes: ECB, CBC, CTR and CCM
    6060  + Bitfield operations
    6061  + thread safe ringbuffer
    6062  + vtimer compatibility layer
    6063 
    6064  Build System
    6065  ------------
    6066  + support for the FIT IoT-LAB testbed by direct integration into the Make build
    6067  system
    6068  + integrated Docker support
    6069  + integration of llvm's clang static analyzer
    6070  + added target for the address sanitizer
    6071  + indicating possible feature conflicts at compile time
    6072  + unified OpenOCD script
    6073 
    6074  Changes
    6075  =======
    6076

    6081  - removed hwtimer
    6082 
    6083  Drivers

    6085  * optimized/remodeled GPIO interface
    6086  * optimized/remodeled TIMER interface
    6087  - temporarily removed CC2420 driver (awaiting last bug fixes for a rewrite)

    6096 
    6097  System libraries
    6098  ----------------
    6099  * new high level UART/stdio interface

    6101  - removed skipjack crypto library

    6104  --------

    6112  Selected Issues Fixed since the Last Release
    6113  ============================================
    6114  #21: Deal with stdin in bordermultiplex.c
    6115  A completely new border router implementation is in place
    6116  #715: test_hwtimer_wait fails on native
    6117  Fixed by @benoit-canet in #2870
    6118  #861: neighbor discovery for 6LoWPAN not working
    6119  GNRC implements 6LoWPAN ND in a RFC6775 compliant way
    6120  #1753: vtimer_msg test crashes after ~49'20" and
    6121  #1449: a removed vtimer might still get called back by hwtimer
    6122  vtimer has been replaced by xtimer which does not have these issues
    6123  #1870: IPv6 neighbor advertisements are malformed
    6124  According to Wireshark (and reference implementations) GNRC sends
    6125  well-formed neighbor advertisements
    6126  #1964 and #1955: eventual problems with IoT-LAB M3 nodes in the testbed
    6127  Solved by new driver versions for UART and radio
    6128  #2228: samd21 stack sizes are too small
    6129  The stacksize has been adapted in #2229
    6130 
    6131  Known Issues
    6132  ============
    6133 
    6134  network related issues
    6135  ----------------------
    6136  #3075: nhdp: unnecessary microsecond precision
    6137  NHDP works with timer values of microsecond precision which is not
    6138  required. Changing to lower precision would save some memory.
    6139  #3086: Max. packet length for AT86RF2XX
    6140  The size of the link-layer header is not dynamically calculated, but
    6141  instead the maximum# size is always assumed.
    6142  #3201: Odd length packet snips cause invalid check sum
    6143  If an odd length packet snip occurs in a packet and is not the last snip
    6144  (in the order the packet is supposed to be, not in the list's order) in a
    6145  packet it will generate a wrong check sum.
    6146  #4048: potential racey memory leak
    6147  According to the packet buffer stats, flood-pinging a multicast destination
    6148  may lead to a memory leak due to a race condition. However, it seems to be
    6149  a rare case and a completely filled up packet buffer was not observed.
    6150 
    6151  native related issues
    6152  ---------------------
    6153  #495: native not float safe
    6154  When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either the
    6155  stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    6156  #499: native is segfaulting on heavy network usage
    6157  Sending more than 100 packets per second causes a SEGFAULT in RIOT native.
    6158  #534: native debugging on osx fails
    6159  Using valgrind or gdb with a nativenet target in OSX leads to "the network"
    6160  being stuck (gdb) or the whole process being stuck (valgrind).
    6161  #3341 and #3824: nativenet crashes when hammered
    6162  Flood-pinging a native instance from more than one host (either multiple
    6163  threads on the host system or multiple other native instances), leads to a
    6164  SEGFAULT.
    6165 
    6166  other platform related issues
    6167  -----------------------------
    6168  #2724: Add support for serial number passing to CMSIS boards, document it
    6169  Documentation about how to discover and set the serial number of CMSIS-DAP
    6170  chips is missing
    6171 
    6172  other issues
    6173  ------------
    6174  #2761: core: define default flags
    6175  If a thread is created without the corresponding flag (CREATE_STACKTEST),
    6176  the ps command will yield wrong numbers for the stack usage
    6177  #2927: core: Automatically select the lowest possible LPM mode
    6178  Not all available low power modes (LPMs) are implemented for each platform
    6179  and the concept of how the LPM is chosen need some reconsideration
    6180  #2967: Makefile.features: location is not relevant for all features
    6181  Provided features for the build system should be split up into a board and
    6182  cpu specific part
    6183  #3109: periph/random: random_read should return unsigned int
    6184  The documentation of this function does not match corresponding
    6185  implementation.

    6225 # Release 2014.12 {#release-2014-12}
    6226 
    6227  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    6228  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: from 8-bit
    6229  microcontrollers to light-weight 32-bit processors.
    6230 
    6231  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    6232  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    6233  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    6234  compliance).

    6348  Fixed Issues from the last release
    6349  ==================================
    6350  #426: Interrupt handling on MSP430 is buggy
    6351  Several fixes by @rousselk
    6352  #1798: core: first thread on runqueue is scheduled twice
    6353  Was fixed along with the thread_yield() refactoring
    6354  #1127: Random build fails on OSX
    6355  native is building stable also on OSX now
    6356 
    6357  Known Issues
    6358  ============
    6359  network related issues
    6360  ----------------------
    6361  #21: Deal with stdin in bordermultiplex.c
    6362  Not all supported platforms provide a stdin in the current release.
    6363  However, the implementation of the 6LoWPAN border router won't work
    6364  without stdin.
    6365  #861: neighbor discovery for 6LoWPAN not working
    6366  Duplicate address detection according to RFC 6775 is also missing.
    6367  #1577: ccn-lite: populate does not work with disabled cache
    6368  If cache is set to zero, the chunks cannot be loaded and therefore also not get populated.
    6369  #1870: IPv6 neighbor advertisements are malformed
    6370  According to Wireshark, ICMPv6 neighbor advertisements are malformed (wrong
    6371  checksum or other reasons).
    6372 
    6373  native related issues
    6374  ---------------------
    6375  #495: native not float safe
    6376  When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either the
    6377  stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    6378  #499: native is segfaulting on heavy network usage
    6379  Sending more than 100 packets per second causes a SEGFAULT in RIOT native.
    6380  #534: native debugging on osx fails
    6381  Using valgrind or gdb with a nativenet target in OSX leads to "the network"
    6382  being stuck (gdb) or the whole process being stuck (valgrind).
    6383  #715: test_hwtimer_wait fails on native
    6384  The problem appears to be lost signals and depends on the CPU speed.
    6385  #787: reboot not working with open file descriptors on native
    6386  If for example a tap device is in use, the reboot command fails.
    6387  #862: sometimes the tap bridge does not work in native
    6388  Sometimes (rather suddenly) packages are not received by a TAP and won't be
    6389  received even if I reconfigure the bridge.
    6390 
    6391  other platform related issues
    6392  -----------------------------
    6393  #1232: x86 doesn't build on OS X with clang
    6394  Current version of the x86 port doesn't build for OS X with clang.
    6395  #1442: setting channel is not persistent cc2420
    6396  After changing the channel via a shell command, the channel reverts back to an arbitrary
    6397  value. However, this might be only a shell problem.
    6398  #1753: vtimer_msg test crashes after ~49'20"
    6399  dependent on the platform, vtimer stops working after some time.
    6400  #1891: printf formatting does not work properly on some Cortex platforms for 64 bit numbers
    6401  This problem happens mostly for the Newlib nano, which does not support 64 bit integer
    6402  printing, but sometimes happens also with other toolchains.
    6403  #1964 and #1955: eventual problems with IoT-LAB M3 nodes in the testbed
    6404  The shell is sometimes not properly working after a reboot and the PDR is sometimes
    6405  worse than expected.
    6406  #2143: tests.core doesn't compile for all platforms
    6407  For some missing GCC compiler builtins, the unittests do not compile for MSP430
    6408  platforms.
    6409  #2228: samd21 stack sizes are too small
    6410  The application examples/default for example will crash when issuing the txtsnd command
    6411 
    6412  other issues:
    6413  --------------
    6414  #1449: a removed vtimer might still get called back by hwtimer
    6415  The timer callback might still fire even after vtimer_remove() was called.
    6416  #2175: valgrind registeres "Invalid write of size 4" in unittests for ubjson
    6417  According to valgrind the stack gets corrupted in UBJSON.
    6418

    6420  https://github.com/RIOT-OS/RIOT/issues

    6451 # Release 2014.05 {#release-2014-05}
    6452 
    6453  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    6454  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: from 16-bit
    6455  microcontrollers to light-weight 32-bit processors.
    6456 
    6457  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    6458  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    6459  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    6460  compliance).
    6461 
    6462  New features
    6463  ============
    6464  Core
    6465  ----
    6466  + introduced explicit core/cpu interface through a set of header files
    6467  + added reboot and panic functions
    6468  + added a node name to the sysconfig struct
    6469  + added the ability to send a message to the current thread's message queue
    6470 
    6471  Supported platforms
    6472  -------------------
    6473  Additional support for the following boards:
    6474  + Arduino Due
    6475  + UDOO board
    6476  + X86 via qemu
    6477  + Zolertia Z1
    6478 
    6479  Network stack
    6480  -------------
    6481  + added net_if as abstraction layer between transceiver module and L3 protocol
    6482  + added support for auto initializing of the 6LoWPAN network stack
    6483  + added support for RFC5444 via oonf_api (from OLSR.org)
    6484  + added a Wireshark dissector for nativenet packets
    6485  + introduced low-level radio driver interface
    6486  + added a default transceiver for all boards
    6487  + common IEEE 802.15.4 radio driver API definition
    6488  + added standard way to query CCA (Clear Channel Assessment) status
    6489  + enabled nonces in interests for CCN-lite (Content Centric Networking)
    6490  + added a route shell command
    6491 
    6492  System libraries
    6493  ----------------
    6494  + added quad-precision math library (quad_math)
    6495 
    6496  Automated Testing
    6497  -----------------
    6498  + added Travis CI based build tests
    6499  + added support for a Jenkins CI server
    6500  + added a unittest framework (based on embunit)
    6501  + added unittests for most core functions
    6502 
    6503  POSIX compliance
    6504  ----------------
    6505  + pthread support including
    6506  + dynamic memory pool and cleanup handlers
    6507  + mutexes
    6508  + condition variable implementation
    6509  + reader/writer lock
    6510  + pthread_barrier_* functions
    6511 
    6512  Native
    6513  ------
    6514  + added a valgrind and cachegrind targets
    6515  + added profiling support
    6516 
    6517  Changes
    6518  =======
    6519  Core
    6520  ----
    6521  * initialize hwtimer automatically
    6522  * optimized thread status field usage
    6523  * moved oneway_malloc to sys
    6524  * prefixed API functions correctly
    6525 
    6526  Network stack
    6527  -------------
    6528  * major refactoring and decoupling
    6529  * refactor use of vtimer
    6530  * fixed forwarding
    6531  * added IoT-LAB M3 Open Node support and dropped TelosB support temporarily for OpenWSN
    6532  * moved ETX beaconing to a module on its own
    6533  * various byte order and other bug fixes
    6534 
    6535  Drivers
    6536  -------
    6537  * added low-level driver interface for unified CPU peripheral abstraction for
    6538  GPIO, ADC, PWM, Timer and UART
    6539  * handle race conditions preventing timers to be set correctly on MSP430 MCUs
    6540  * several CC2420 fixes
    6541 
    6542  System libraries
    6543  ----------------
    6544  * auto_init is used by default
    6545  * changed function prototype for shell handlers
    6546 
    6547  Other
    6548  -----
    6549  * cleaned up Makefile system and simplified binary directory
    6550  * improved documentation for core and sys
    6551  * build system uses PKG dependency
    6552  * build system sets include paths automatically
    6553  * black and white lists for applications and tests
    6554  * add stacksize checker for DEBUG macro
    6555  * styling corrections
    6556  * fixed license boiler plates
    6557  * set lpc2k_pgm return value correctly
    6558  * various bug fixes and cleanups
    6559 
    6560  Fixed Issues from the last release
    6561  ==================================
    6562  #45: bit field order in the fcf may be wrong
    6563  The CC2420 FIFO expects the IEEE802.15.4 FCF field in reversed bit order.
    6564  With this release the byte order is now handled by the net_if module and
    6565  all device specific handling is done by the driver.
    6566  #82: Setting STATUS_REPLY_BLOCKED thread to STATUS_PENDING though it is not
    6567  handled yet
    6568  In some rare cases the status of a thread might falsely change to
    6569  STATUS_PENDING instead of STATUS_REPLY_BLOCKED.
    6570  #455: sha256 is broken on MSP430
    6571  Fixed.
    6572  #498: native is segfaulting at startup
    6573  Fixed by several PRs (#501, #583, and #588).
    6574  #505: native on FreeBSD is broken
    6575  Fixed by PR #1022.
    6576 
    6577  Known Issues
    6578  ============
    6579  network related issues
    6580  ----------------------
    6581  #21: Deal with stdin in bordermultiplex.c
    6582  Not all supported platforms provide a stdin in the current release.
    6583  However, the implementation of the 6LoWPAN border router won't work
    6584  without stdin.
    6585  #861: neighbor discovery for 6LoWPAN not working
    6586  Duplicate address detection according to RFC 6775 is also missing.
    6587 
    6588  native related issues
    6589  ---------------------
    6590  #495: native not float safe
    6591  When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either the
    6592  stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    6593  #499: native is segfaulting on heavy network usage
    6594  Sending more than 100 packets per second causes a SEGFAULT in RIOT native.
    6595  #534: native debugging on osx fails
    6596  Using valgrind or gdb with a nativenet target in OSX leads to "the network"
    6597  being stuck (gdb) or the whole process being stuck (valgrind).
    6598  #715: test_hwtimer_wait fails on native
    6599  The problem appears to be lost signals and depends on the CPU speed.
    6600  #787: reboot not working with open file descriptors on native
    6601  If for example a tap device is in use, the reboot command fails.
    6602  #862: sometimes the tap bridge does not work in native
    6603  Sometimes (rather suddenly) packages are not received by a TAP and won't be
    6604  received even if I reconfigure the bridge.
    6605  #1127: Random build fails on OSX
    6606  Building for native on OSX often fails - Workaround: build using -B flag,
    6607  e.g.: make -B clean all
    6608 
    6609  other platform related issues
    6610  -----------------------------
    6611  #426: Interrupt handling on MSP430 is buggy
    6612  UART and timer handling is currently unstable on MSP430 based platforms
    6613  #1232: x86 doesn't build on OS X with clang
    6614  Current version of the x86 port doesn't build for OS X with clang.
    6615 
    6616  For all issues and open pull requests please check the RIOT issue tracker:
    6617  https://github.com/RIOT-OS/RIOT/issues
    6618

    6644 # Release 2014.01 {#release-2014-01}
    6645 
    6646  RIOT is a real-time multi-threading operating system that supports a range of
    6647  devices that are typically found in the Internet of Things: from 16-bit
    6648  microcontrollers to light-weight 32-bit processors.
    6649 
    6650  RIOT is based on the following design principles: energy-efficiency, real-time
    6651  capabilities, small memory footprint, modularity, and uniform API access,
    6652  independent of the underlying hardware (this API offers partial POSIX
    6653  compliance).
    6654 
    6655  New features
    6656  ============
    6657  Core
    6658  ----
    6659  + msg_receive() with timeout
    6660  + LPM support for MSP430 based platforms
    6661  + introduced a version string
    6662 
    6663  Supported platforms
    6664  -------------------
    6665  Additional support for the following boards:
    6666  + TelosB
    6667  + mbed LPC1768
    6668 
    6669  Sensor drivers
    6670  ---------------
    6671  + drivers for the LM75A Digital temperature sensor and thermal watchdog
    6672  + SRF02 and SRF08 ultrasonic range finders
    6673 
    6674  Native port
    6675  -----------
    6676  + implemented UART via I/O redirection or TCP and UNIX socket
    6677 
    6678  System libraries
    6679  ----------------
    6680  + Mersenne twister pseudorandom number generator
    6681  + crypto libraries
    6682  + 3des
    6683  + aes
    6684  + rc5
    6685  + skipjack
    6686  + twofish
    6687  + BSD-like package system for easy integration of external libraries
    6688 
    6689  Network stack
    6690  -------------
    6691  + port of CCN lite
    6692  + POSIX socket wrapper
    6693  + integration of libcoap
    6694  + integration of OpenWSN
    6695 
    6696  Further Changes
    6697  ===============
    6698  * boards and projects repositories have been integrated and are now part of
    6699  the RIOT repository itself
    6700  * full refactoring of the network stack and introducing a substructure
    6701  according to the modules' functionalities
    6702  * cleaned up Makefile system and simplified binary directory
    6703  * more documentation
    6704  * various bug fixes and cleanups
    6705 
    6706  Fixed Issues from the last release
    6707  ==================================
    6708  #45: bit field order in the fcf may be wrong
    6709  The CC2420 FIFO expects the IEEE802.15.4 FCF field in reversed bit order.
    6710  With this release the byte order is now handled by the net_if module and
    6711  all device specific handling is done by the driver.
    6712  #82: Setting STATUS_REPLY_BLOCKED thread to STATUS_PENDING though it is not
    6713  handled yet
    6714  Pull Request #569 fixed this bug by checking for STATUS_REPLY_BLOCKED in
    6715  msg_receive().
    6716  #455: sha256 is broken on MSP430
    6717  The problem was caused
    6718 
    6719  Known Issues
    6720  ============
    6721  #21: Deal with stdin in bordermultiplex.c
    6722  Not all supported platforms provide a stdin in the current release.
    6723  However, the implementation of the 6LoWPAN border router won't work
    6724  without stdin.
    6725  #426: Interrupt handling on MSP430 is buggy
    6726  UART and timer handling is still unstable on MSP430 based platforms.
    6727  #495: native not float safe
    6728  When the FPU is used when an asynchronous context switch occurs, either the
    6729  stack gets corrupted or a floating point exception occurs.
    6730  #498: native is segfaulting at startup
    6731  In some cases (about 5-10%) a RIOT native process crashes with a SEGFAULT
    6732  at startup.
    6733  #499: native is segfaulting on heavy network usage
    6734  Sending more than 100 packets per second causes a SEGFAULT in RIOT native.
    6735  #505: native on FreeBSD is broken
    6736  Due to different parameter handling in FreeBSD, native is currently not
    6737  working there.
    6738 
    6739  For all issues and open pull requests please check the RIOT issue tracker:
    6740  https://github.com/RIOT-OS/RIOT/issues

    6742 # Release 2013.08 {#release-2013-08}
    6743 
    6744  Kernel
    6745  ------
    6746  - Microkernel with a powerful messaging system
    6747  - Multi-Threading with low overhead
    6748  - an energy-efficient, real-time capable scheduler
    6749  - small memory footprint
    6750 
    6751  Userspace
    6752  ---------
    6753  - 6LoWPAN according to RFC 4944, RFC 6282, and RFC 6775
    6754  - TCP and UDP
    6755  - RPL according to RFC 6550 and RFC 6719
    6756  - High resolution and long-term timers
    6757  - POSIX IO and BSD socket API
    6758  - Bloom filter
    6759  - SHA256
    6760 
    6761  Hardware Support
    6762  ----------------
    6763  - various ARM and MSP430 MCUs
    6764  * ARM7 NXP LPC2387
    6765  * TI MSP430F1612
    6766  * TI CC430F6137
    6767  * ARM7 Freescale MC13224v (preliminary)
    6768  * ARM Cortex-M4 STM32f407vgt6 (preliminary)
    6769  * ARM Cortex-M3 STM32f103rey6 (preliminary)
    6770  - radio drivers
    6771  * TI CC1100 and CC1101
    6772  * TI CC2420
    6773  * Atmel AT86RF231
    6774  - sensor drivers
    6775  * Sensirion SHT11
    6776  * Linear Technology LT4150
    6777
